###begin article-title 0
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 59 73 59 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
fog-2 and the Evolution of Self-Fertile Hermaphroditism in Caenorhabditis
###end article-title 0
###begin article-title 1
The Evolution of Self-Fertile Hermaphroditism: The Fog Is Clearing
###end article-title 1
###begin p 2
###xml 228 250 228 250 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Caenorhabditis elegans</named-content>
###xml 255 267 255 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 272 286 272 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 372 383 372 383 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 411 421 411 421 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 466 471 466 471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 598 609 598 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans,</italic>
###xml 739 744 739 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 776 786 776 786 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 885 888 885 888 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog</italic>
###xml 930 942 930 942 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 974 979 974 979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 1026 1037 1026 1037 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans,</italic>
###xml 1215 1232 1215 1232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae gld-1</italic>
###xml 1513 1518 1513 1518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 1559 1569 1559 1569 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 1574 1586 1574 1586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 1753 1767 1753 1767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 1799 1809 1799 1809 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 228 250 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
###xml 255 266 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 372 383 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 411 421 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 598 608 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 776 786 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 930 941 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 1026 1036 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1215 1226 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 1559 1569 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1574 1585 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 1799 1809 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Somatic and germline sex determination pathways have diverged significantly in animals, making comparisons between taxa difficult. To overcome this difficulty, we compared the genes in the germline sex determination pathways of Caenorhabditis elegans and C. briggsae, two Caenorhabditis species with similar reproductive systems and sequenced genomes. We demonstrate that C. briggsae has orthologs of all known C. elegans sex determination genes with one exception: fog-2. Hermaphroditic nematodes are essentially females that produce sperm early in life, which they use for self fertilization. In C. elegans, this brief period of spermatogenesis requires FOG-2 and the RNA-binding protein GLD-1, which together repress translation of the tra-2 mRNA. FOG-2 is part of a large C. elegans FOG-2-related protein family defined by the presence of an F-box and Duf38/FOG-2 homogy domain. A fog-2-related gene family is also present in C. briggsae, however, the branch containing fog-2 appears to have arisen relatively recently in C. elegans, post-speciation. The C-terminus of FOG-2 is rapidly evolving, is required for GLD-1 interaction, and is likely critical for the role of FOG-2 in sex determination. In addition, C. briggsae gld-1 appears to play the opposite role in sex determination (promoting the female fate) while maintaining conserved roles in meiotic progression during oogenesis. Our data indicate that the regulation of the hermaphrodite germline sex determination pathway at the level of FOG-2/GLD-1/tra-2 mRNA is fundamentally different between C. elegans and C. briggsae, providing functional evidence in support of the independent evolution of self-fertile hermaphroditism. We speculate on the convergent evolution of hermaphroditism in Caenorhabditis based on the plasticity of the C. elegans germline sex determination cascade, in which multiple mutant paths yield self fertility.
###end p 2
###begin p 3
###xml 43 53 43 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 58 69 58 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae</italic>
###xml 166 180 166 180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 43 53 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 58 69 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
A comparison of sex determination genes in C. elegans and C. briggsae provides evidence in support of the convergent evolution of self-fertile hermaphroditism in the Caenorhabditis clade
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Introduction
###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 134 156 134 156 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Caenorhabditis elegans</named-content>
###xml 161 184 161 184 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 313 314 313 314 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b01">1</xref>
###xml 315 316 315 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b02">2</xref>
###xml 317 318 317 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b03">3</xref>
###xml 134 156 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
###xml 161 184 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila melanogaster</span>
Sex determination is an ancient and universal feature in metazoans. In spite of this, comparison of distantly related species such as Caenorhabditis elegans and Drosophila melanogaster has revealed little about the evolution of the complex pathways that mediate the sexual fate decision in the soma and germline [1,2,3]. This is likely due to the combination of gross morphological, functional, and behavioral dissimilarity and extensive sequence divergence. Thus, if we wish to clarify the etiology of diverged sex determination pathways, an alternative approach is required.
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 260 270 260 270 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 275 286 275 286 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 394 404 394 404 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 477 478 477 478 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b04">4</xref>
###xml 479 480 479 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b05">5</xref>
###xml 260 270 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 275 286 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 394 404 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
One approach is to perform comparative analysis of sex determination genes in species separated by sufficient evolutionary time to allow for changes in pathway components yet retain comparable somatic and germline morphology and function. The clade containing C. elegans and C. briggsae represents an ideal case for this type of study, as the sex determination pathway has been well studied in C. elegans and an abundance of sequence information is available for both species [4,5].
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 0 10 0 10 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 15 27 15 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 202 203 202 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b05">5</xref>
###xml 204 205 204 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b06">6</xref>
###xml 206 207 206 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b07">7</xref>
###xml 208 209 208 209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b08">8</xref>
###xml 210 211 210 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b09">9</xref>
###xml 212 214 212 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b10">10</xref>
###xml 217 227 217 227 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 232 243 232 243 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 369 379 369 379 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. remanei</named-content>
###xml 384 386 384 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C.</italic>
###xml 448 449 448 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b06">6</xref>
###xml 450 451 450 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b07">7</xref>
###xml 452 454 452 454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b10">10</xref>
###xml 507 521 507 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 602 612 602 612 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 617 628 617 628 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 666 668 666 668 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b10">10</xref>
###xml 669 671 669 671 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b11">11</xref>
###xml 0 10 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 15 26 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 217 227 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 232 243 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 369 379 <span type="species:ncbi:31234">C. remanei</span>
###xml 602 612 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 617 628 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
C. elegans and C. briggsae, while sharing very similar germline and somatic morphology, are separated by approximately 100 million years and are members of a clade that employs multiple mating systems [5,6,7,8,9,10]. C. elegans and C. briggsae are self-fertile hermaphrodites that maintain males at a low frequency (androdioecious), whereas the morphologically similar C. remanei and C. sp. CB5161 are obligate female/male (gonochoristic) species [6,7,10]. Phylogenetic analysis of the four closely related Caenorhabditis species suggests that self-fertile hermaphroditism has evolved independently in C. elegans and C. briggsae from an ancestral male/female state [10,11]. Importantly, a transition in mating system from female/male to hermaphroditic (or hermaphroditic to male/female) requires that one or more changes in the sex determination pathway have occurred.
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 0 10 0 10 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 15 27 15 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 130 131 130 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b08">8</xref>
###xml 132 134 132 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b12">12</xref>
###xml 135 137 135 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b13">13</xref>
###xml 451 453 451 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b14">14</xref>
###xml 454 456 454 456 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b15">15</xref>
###xml 590 592 590 592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b14">14</xref>
###xml 593 595 593 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b16">16</xref>
###xml 596 598 596 598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b17">17</xref>
###xml 0 10 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 15 26 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
C. elegans and C. briggsae, like many other animals, have two sexes specified by the ratio of X chromosomes to sets of autosomes [8,12,13]. In both species, XX animals are somatically female while the germline is hermaphroditic. Self fertility is achieved by a transient period of spermatogenesis beginning in the third larval (L3) stage before the organism switches to the production of oocytes in the L4 stage, which continues throughout adulthood [14,15]. In both species, XO males begin sperm production in the L3 stage and continue spermatogenesis throughout their reproductive lives [14,16,17].
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 47 57 47 57 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 106 112 106 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2,</italic>
###xml 158 164 158 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3,</italic>
###xml 203 205 203 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b18">18</xref>
###xml 206 208 206 208 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b19">19</xref>
###xml 211 219 211 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 241 246 241 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 251 256 251 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
###xml 439 444 439 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">her-1</italic>
###xml 455 460 455 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 514 519 514 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
###xml 568 570 568 570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b20">20</xref>
###xml 571 573 571 573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b21">21</xref>
###xml 600 605 600 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">her-1</italic>
###xml 643 648 643 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">her-1</italic>
###xml 759 761 759 761 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b22">22</xref>
###xml 762 764 762 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b23">23</xref>
###xml 47 57 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
A major determinant of germline sexual fate in C. elegans is the relative activity of two key regulators: tra-2, which promotes the female fate (oocyte), and fem-3, which promotes the male fate (sperm) [18,19] (Figure 1A). The activities of tra-2 and fem-3 must be regulated in both males and hermaphrodites to allow spermatogenesis to occur, however the mechanisms by which this regulation occurs differs between the two sexes. In males, her-1 represses tra-2 feminizing activity and raises the relative level of fem-3 activity so that spermatogenesis is continuous [20,21]. Since null mutations in her-1 have no effect on hermaphrodites and her-1 is not expressed in XX animals, a different mechanism is used to allow for the transient production of sperm [22,23].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 18 28 18 28 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 135 143 135 143 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 255 260 255 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 278 283 278 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1</italic>
###xml 326 331 326 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 361 363 361 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b24">24</xref>
###xml 364 366 364 366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 369 377 369 377 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 383 384 383 384 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">1</xref>
###xml 428 433 428 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 483 488 483 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
###xml 540 548 540 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 622 633 622 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2/gld-1</italic>
###xml 657 662 657 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 711 716 711 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
###xml 743 748 743 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mog-1</italic>
###xml 752 775 752 775 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mog-6, fbf-1 and fbf-2,</italic>
###xml 780 785 780 785 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nos-1</italic>
###xml 789 794 789 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nos-3</italic>
###xml 796 798 796 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b18">18</xref>
###xml 799 801 799 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b19">19</xref>
###xml 802 804 802 804 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b26">26</xref>
###xml 18 28 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Self fertility in C. elegans hermaphrodites is achieved by an early period of spermatogenesis followed by a later period of oogenesis (Figure 1A). The promotion of spermatogenesis during the L3 stage (early) is achieved by translational repression of the tra-2 mRNA mediated by gld-1 ("defective in germline development") and fog-2 ("feminization of germline")[24,25] (Figure 1A and 1B). The transient reduction in the level of tra-2 feminizing activity raises the relative level of fem-3 masculinizing activity to promote spermatogenesis (Figure 1A). Later in L4 and adult animals, oogenesis is promoted by relieving the fog-2/gld-1-mediated repression of tra-2 feminizing activity combined with repression of fem-3 masculinizing activity by mog-1 to mog-6, fbf-1 and fbf-2, and nos-1 to nos-3 [18,19,26].
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 35 40 35 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 45 57 45 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1. fog-2</italic>
###xml 122 133 122 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans,</italic>
###xml 158 163 158 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b27">27</xref>
###xml 298 303 298 303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1</italic>
###xml 386 388 386 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b28">28</xref>
###xml 389 391 389 391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b29">29</xref>
###xml 399 404 399 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 409 414 409 414 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1</italic>
###xml 587 589 587 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 590 592 590 592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b27">27</xref>
###xml 593 595 593 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b28">28</xref>
###xml 596 598 596 598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b29">29</xref>
###xml 599 601 599 601 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b30">30</xref>
###xml 122 132 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Central to this work are the genes fog-2 and gld-1. fog-2 is required for hermaphrodite, but not male, spermatogenesis in C. elegans, as XX animals that lack fog-2 produce only oocytes, resulting in functional females, whereas XO males are unaffected [27]. Similarly, loss-of-function mutations in gld-1 result in the feminization of the hermaphrodite germline without affecting males [28,29]. Both fog-2 and gld-1 are germline-specific regulators of sexual fate, since they do not appear to be expressed in the soma, and null mutations in either gene do not affect somatic sexual fate [25,27,28,29,30].
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 0 16 0 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans gld-1</italic>
###xml 94 96 94 96 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b28">28</xref>
###xml 97 99 97 99 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b29">29</xref>
###xml 154 156 154 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b30">30</xref>
###xml 231 233 231 233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b31">31</xref>
###xml 246 252 246 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2,</italic>
###xml 294 299 294 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 375 380 375 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 387 389 387 389 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b24">24</xref>
###xml 390 392 390 392 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b32">32</xref>
###xml 395 403 395 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 423 428 423 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 563 565 563 565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b20">20</xref>
###xml 566 568 566 568 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 569 571 569 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b33">33</xref>
###xml 572 574 572 574 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b34">34</xref>
###xml 0 10 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
C. elegans gld-1 is a germline-specific tumor suppressor that is indispensable for oogenesis [28,29] and encodes a conserved KH-type RNA-binding protein [30]. GLD-1 is a translational repressor that binds to multiple mRNA targets [31], including tra-2, where it binds as a dimer to each of two tra-2 and GLI elements (TGEs) present on the 3' untranslated region (UTR) of the tra-2 mRNA [24,32] (Figure 1B). Deletion of the tra-2 TGEs results in a loss of GLD-1-mediated translational control and feminization of the germline, such that only oocytes are produced [20,25,33,34].
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 0 10 0 10 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 300 302 300 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b35">35</xref>
###xml 337 339 337 339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 549 551 549 551 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b36">36</xref>
###xml 667 669 667 669 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 672 680 672 680 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 741 746 741 746 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 805 810 805 810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 904 906 904 906 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b24">24</xref>
###xml 907 909 907 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 912 920 912 920 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 0 10 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
C. elegans FOG-2 was identified as a GLD-1-interacting protein with a structure similar to canonical F-box proteins; it has an N-terminal F-box and a C-terminal protein-protein interaction domain. In the case of FOG-2 the putative protein-protein interaction domain is referred to as Duf38 (Pfam in [35]) or FOG-2 homology domain (FTH) [25]. F-box proteins are often core components of the Skp1/Cullin/F-box-type E3 ubiquitin ligase complexes, and they serve to link specific substrates to the ubiquitin ligase machinery for subsequent proteolysis [36]. However, FOG-2 cannot target GLD-1 for degradation since both function to promote hermaphrodite spermatogenesis [25] (Figure 1A). Current data suggest that the formation of a FOG-2/GLD-1/tra-2 mRNA ternary complex mediates translational repression of tra-2 and a corresponding reduction in feminizing activity to allow hermaphrodite spermatogenesis [24,25] (Figure 1B).
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 22 32 22 32 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 50 51 50 51 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b04">4</xref>
###xml 143 154 143 154 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 156 157 156 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b05">5</xref>
###xml 334 344 334 344 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 349 360 349 360 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 22 32 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 143 154 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 334 344 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 349 360 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The completion of the C. elegans genome sequence [4] and the 10X sequence (representing more than 98% coverage) of the closely related species C. briggsae [5] permits studies of the evolution of sex determination and the inception of hermaphrodite spermatogenesis in morphologically comparable species. Here, we pose the question, do C. elegans and C. briggsae specify male sexual fate in the hermaphrodite germline similarly?
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 22 32 22 32 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 62 73 62 73 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 196 201 196 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 259 269 259 269 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 363 368 363 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 406 411 406 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 435 446 435 446 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 517 522 517 522 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1</italic>
###xml 535 546 535 546 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 656 666 656 666 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 692 709 692 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae fog-2</italic>
###xml 776 787 776 787 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 22 32 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 62 73 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 259 269 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 435 446 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 535 546 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 656 666 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 692 703 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 776 787 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
We find that 30 of 31 C. elegans sex determination genes have C. briggsae orthologs, indicating that there is extensive conservation of sex determination pathway components; the lone exception is fog-2. We provide evidence that the essential role of FOG-2 in C. elegans hermaphrodite spermatogenesis evolved from post-speciation duplication and divergence of the fog-2-related (FTR) gene family and that a fog-2 gene is not present in C. briggsae. Furthermore, double-stranded-RNA-mediated interference (RNAi) of the gld-1 ortholog in C. briggsae results in masculinization of the germline instead of the feminization of the germline phenotype observed in C. elegans. The lack of a potential C. briggsae fog-2 combined with the opposite sex determination function of GLD-1 in C. briggsae indicate that the control of hermaphrodite spermatogenesis, while using most of the same gene products, is fundamentally different between the species and is likely to have evolved independently.
###end p 15
###begin title 16
Results
###end title 16
###begin title 17
###xml 62 72 62 72 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 77 88 77 88 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 62 72 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 77 88 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Components of Sex Determination Pathway Are Conserved between C. elegans and C. briggsae
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 64 74 64 74 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 79 90 79 90 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 122 124 122 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b37">37</xref>
###xml 125 127 125 127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b38">38</xref>
###xml 128 130 128 130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b39">39</xref>
###xml 154 165 154 165 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 188 198 188 198 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 568 578 568 578 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 582 593 582 593 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 682 689 682 689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0030006-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 850 852 850 852 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b17">17</xref>
###xml 853 855 853 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b26">26</xref>
###xml 856 858 856 858 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b40">40</xref>
###xml 859 861 859 861 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b41">41</xref>
###xml 862 864 862 864 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b42">42</xref>
###xml 865 867 865 867 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b43">43</xref>
###xml 868 870 868 870 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b44">44</xref>
###xml 903 908 903 908 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 64 74 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 79 90 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 154 165 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 188 198 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 568 578 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 582 593 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
To survey conservation in the sex determination pathway between C. elegans and C. briggsae we used reciprocal best BLAST [37,38,39] to identify potential C. briggsae orthologs of 31 known C. elegans sex determination genes, some of which have been previously identified. The 31 genes included 16 that function only in germline sex determination, seven that function in both somatic and germline sex determination, two that function only in somatic sex determination, and six that coordinate sex determination and dosage compensation. We found that 30 of 31 genes have C. elegans-to-C. briggsae reciprocal best BLAST hits and alignments consistent with a high level of conservation (Table 1). Using this method, putative orthologs of all known sex determination genes, including less conserved members, and previously identified genes were recovered [17,26,40,41,42,43,44], with the notable exception of fog-2.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 23 34 23 34 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 172 182 172 182 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 187 198 187 198 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 200 205 200 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">her-1</italic>
###xml 207 209 207 209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b43">43</xref>
###xml 212 217 212 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 219 221 219 221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b21">21</xref>
###xml 224 229 224 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-1</italic>
###xml 267 272 267 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-2</italic>
###xml 274 276 274 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b45">45</xref>
###xml 279 284 279 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
###xml 286 288 286 288 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b41">41</xref>
###xml 291 296 291 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-3</italic>
###xml 298 300 298 300 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b42">42</xref>
###xml 307 312 307 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-1</italic>
###xml 314 316 314 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b17">17</xref>
###xml 417 422 417 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 427 433 427 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3,</italic>
###xml 514 516 514 516 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b21">21</xref>
###xml 517 519 517 519 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b41">41</xref>
###xml 522 530 522 530 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 792 802 792 802 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 807 818 807 818 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 901 912 901 912 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 960 970 960 970 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 23 34 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 172 182 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 187 198 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 792 802 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 807 818 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 901 912 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 960 970 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The functions of seven C. briggsae sex determination genes have been tested, and current data indicate that these genes exhibit similar and possibly identical functions in C. elegans and C. briggsae (her-1 [43], tra-2 [21], fem-1 [A. Spence, personal communication], fem-2 [45], fem-3 [41], fog-3 [42], and tra-1 [17]). Importantly, the epistatic relationship and function of two key regulators of sex determination, tra-2 and fem-3, are essentially intact between the sister species in somatic sex determination [21,41] (Figure 1A). At first glance, given the conservation of 30/31 sex determination genes, similar or identical functions for 7/7 genes tested, and maintenance of a key epistatic relationship, it would appear that the sex determination pathway is generally conserved between C. elegans and C. briggsae. However, genetic and molecular studies will be required to determine whether the C. briggsae orthologs are functionally equivalent to their C. elegans counterparts.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 127 129 127 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b46">46</xref>
###xml 296 301 296 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 376 387 376 387 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 413 423 413 423 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 459 470 459 470 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 376 387 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 413 423 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 459 470 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
A single FOG-2 ortholog could not be resolved by reciprocal best BLAST or by using the reciprocal smallest distance algorithm [46], which uses global sequence alignment and maximum likelihood estimation of evolutionary distances, to infer putative orthologs (data not shown). This indicates that fog-2 is either highly diverged, present in an unsequenced portion (<2%) of the C. briggsae genome, or potentially a C. elegans-specific adaptation not present in C. briggsae.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 11 21 11 21 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 11 21 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
fog-2 Is a C. elegans-Specific Adaptation
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 92 102 92 102 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 159 161 159 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 162 164 162 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b36">36</xref>
###xml 202 214 202 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 375 385 375 385 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 390 401 390 401 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 425 435 425 435 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 440 451 440 451 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 694 696 694 696 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b47">47</xref>
###xml 92 102 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 202 213 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 375 385 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 390 401 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 425 435 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 440 451 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
FOG-2 is part of a large, highly diverged F-box- and DUF38/FTH-containing protein family in C. elegans with more than 100 members referred to as FTR proteins [25,36]. The FTR family is also expanded in C. briggsae, making the identification of a single functionally equivalent ortholog from a large number of paralogs difficult. Therefore, to discern the relationships among C. elegans and C. briggsae FTR family members, 30 C. elegans and C. briggsae FTR proteins or protein predictions closely related to FOG-2 were used to generate a neighbor-joining phylogeny. The remaining, more diverged FTR members from either species were not included in the phylogeny to avoid long branch attraction [47].
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 4 14 4 14 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 19 30 19 30 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 69 79 69 79 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 131 142 131 142 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 213 223 213 223 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 228 239 228 239 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 274 282 274 282 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 386 395 386 395 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="sg001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 429 439 429 439 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 462 473 462 473 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 531 541 531 541 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 601 611 601 611 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 616 627 616 627 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 757 767 757 767 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 772 783 772 783 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 4 14 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 19 30 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 69 79 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 131 142 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 213 223 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 228 239 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 429 439 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 462 473 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 531 541 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 601 611 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 616 627 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 757 767 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 772 783 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The C. elegans and C. briggsae FTR phylogeny reveals that all of the C. elegans FOG-2 relatives form a single clade and all of the C. briggsae relatives a distinct clade. An unrooted radial phylogram illustrating C. elegans and C. briggsae FTR relationships is presented in Figure 2, and a rectangular representation of the same phylogeny with bootstrap support information is shown in Figure S1. If a closely related homolog of C. elegans FOG-2 were present in C. briggsae the expectation is that it would have clustered with the C. elegans proteins. Contrary to this, the phylogenetic separation of C. elegans and C. briggsae FTR family members into distinct lineages indicates that extensive expansion in the FTR family occurred post-speciation and that C. elegans and C. briggsae FTR genes do not have one-to-one orthologous relationships.
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 59 76 59 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae fog-2</italic>
###xml 193 198 193 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 472 477 472 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 524 535 524 535 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 611 616 611 616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 768 779 768 779 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae</italic>
###xml 781 794 781 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2, her-1,</italic>
###xml 799 804 799 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-2</italic>
###xml 834 845 834 845 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 863 865 863 865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b40">40</xref>
###xml 866 868 866 868 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b43">43</xref>
###xml 869 871 869 871 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b44">44</xref>
###xml 59 70 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 524 535 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 768 779 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 834 845 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The above results could be misleading if a closely related C. briggsae fog-2 homolog were present in the less than 2% of the genome sequence that is not present in the final assembly or if the fog-2 ortholog diverged sufficiently such that the computational methods were not able to distinguish between orthologous and paralogous relationships. To address these possibilities we used low-stringency cross-species Southern blotting in an effort to identify closely related fog-2-like sequences in unsequenced portions of the C. briggsae genome, and we used conserved synteny in an attempt to identify a diverged fog-2 ortholog that might reside in the same genomic location. Both approaches were used to effectively identify other diverged sex determination genes from C. briggsae (tra-2, her-1, and fem-2) prior to the release of the C. briggsae genome sequence [40,43,44].
###end p 24
###begin p 25
###xml 47 63 47 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans fog-2</italic>
###xml 76 81 76 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-2</italic>
###xml 113 124 113 124 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 206 222 206 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans fem-2</italic>
###xml 237 248 237 248 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 262 264 262 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b40">40</xref>
###xml 270 281 270 281 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 311 327 311 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans fog-2</italic>
###xml 335 343 335 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 381 386 381 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 438 449 438 449 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 535 540 535 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-2</italic>
###xml 47 57 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 113 124 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 206 216 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 237 248 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 270 281 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 311 321 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 438 449 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
For low-stringency Southern blotting we used a C. elegans fog-2 probe and a fem-2 positive control probe against C. briggsae genomic DNA. Under conditions that detected cross-species hybridization with the C. elegans fem-2 probe against C. briggsae genomic DNA [40], no C. briggsae signal was observed with the C. elegans fog-2 probe (Figure 3A). This suggests either that a close fog-2 relative is not present in the less than 2% of the C. briggsae genome that is unsequenced or that it has diverged significantly beyond the level of fem-2.
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 65 75 65 75 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 94 99 94 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 101 123 101 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srg-34, sec-23, psa-1,</italic>
###xml 171 182 171 182 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 202 217 202 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srg-34, sec-23,</italic>
###xml 222 227 222 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">psa-1</italic>
###xml 305 316 305 316 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 318 326 318 326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 332 333 332 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">3</xref>
###xml 413 429 413 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans fog-2</italic>
###xml 481 492 481 492 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 494 502 494 502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 508 509 508 509 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">3</xref>
###xml 588 599 588 599 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 749 757 749 757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 763 764 763 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">3</xref>
###xml 777 782 777 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 891 902 891 902 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 972 974 972 974 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="st001">S1</xref>
###xml 979 981 979 981 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="st002">S2</xref>
###xml 65 75 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 171 182 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 305 316 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 413 423 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 481 492 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 588 599 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 891 902 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
For analysis of conserved syntenic relationships, five conserved C. elegans genes surrounding fog-2 (srg-34, sec-23, psa-1, Y113G7A.14, and Y113G7B.15) were used to query C. briggsae contigs. The genes srg-34, sec-23, and psa-1 are highly conserved across metazoans and have reciprocal best BLAST hits in C. briggsae (Figure 3B and 3C, small arrow heads). The genes Y113G7A.14 and Y113G7B.15 flank the gene-dense C. elegans fog-2 region and also have reciprocal best BLAST hits in C. briggsae (Figure 3B and 3C, large arrow heads). All five genes were found to be represented on a single C. briggsae contig, suggesting that the global syntenic relationships are conserved, but with detailed analysis revealing a number of differences in gene order (Figure 3B and 3C). However, fog-2, its four adjacent close FTR relatives, and 16 surrounding genes in an 82.6-kb region were absent from this C. briggsae contig, while the conserved genes on either side were present (Table S1 and S2).
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 24 29 24 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 42 48 42 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1,</italic>
###xml 98 101 98 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr</italic>
###xml 129 139 129 139 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 159 170 159 170 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 172 174 172 174 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 177 186 177 186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 191 192 191 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g003">3</xref>
###xml 198 203 198 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 208 213 208 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1</italic>
###xml 282 292 282 292 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 392 393 392 393 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 417 422 417 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 427 432 427 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1</italic>
###xml 451 473 451 473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans/C. briggsae</italic>
###xml 539 540 539 540 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 545 556 545 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2/ftr-1</italic>
###xml 576 577 576 577 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 607 608 607 608 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 648 658 648 658 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 663 673 663 673 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggse</named-content>
###xml 689 690 689 690 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 700 701 700 701 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b05">5</xref>
###xml 129 139 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 159 170 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 282 292 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 451 461 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 462 473 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 648 658 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The closest relative of fog-2 is the gene ftr-1, which is part of a group of five closely related ftr genes that are colinear in C. elegans and not present in C. briggsae [25] (Figures 2 and 3). If fog-2 and ftr-1 are the result of a "recent" post-speciation duplication within the C. elegans lineage, as suggested by the phylogeny, then we would expect that fewer synonymous substitutions (Ks) have occurred between fog-2 and ftr-1 relative to other C. elegans/C. briggsae best BLAST orthologs. Consistent with a recent duplication, the Ks for fog-2/ftr-1 is not saturated (Ks = 0.36) whereas the average Ks for reciprocal best BLAST hits between C. elegans and C. briggse is saturated (Ks = 1.72) [5].
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 17 22 17 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 27 32 27 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1</italic>
###xml 89 99 89 99 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 138 143 138 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 162 173 162 173 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 200 211 200 211 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 273 283 273 283 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 89 99 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 162 173 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 200 211 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 273 283 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The finding that fog-2 and ftr-1 arose from a relatively recent local duplication within C. elegans strongly supports the contention that fog-2 is not present in C. briggsae. These results imply that C. briggsae must regulate hermaphrodite spermatogenesis differently than C. elegans.
###end p 28
###begin title 29
The Diverged C-Terminal of FOG-2 Is Necessary for GLD-1 Binding
###end title 29
###begin p 30
###xml 62 67 62 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 169 174 169 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 253 255 253 255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b24">24</xref>
###xml 256 258 256 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 301 306 301 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 311 316 311 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1</italic>
###xml 318 326 318 326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 329 334 329 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1</italic>
###xml 357 362 357 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 414 416 414 416 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 439 444 439 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
Previous work has shown that FOG-2 is an integral part of the tra-2 3' UTR translational repression complex. The RNA-binding protein GLD-1 makes direct contact with the tra-2 3' UTR, and FOG-2 is recruited to the complex via its interaction with GLD-1 [24,25]. In spite of the high similarity between fog-2 and ftr-1 (Figure 4), ftr-1 cannot compensate for fog-2 in the promotion of hermaphrodite spermatogenesis [25]. This indicates that fog-2 must contain unique sequences that allow it to function in sex determination.
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 124 132 124 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 134 135 134 135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g004">4</xref>
###xml 218 223 218 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 228 233 228 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1</italic>
###xml 519 527 519 527 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 533 534 533 534 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g004">4</xref>
###xml 582 587 582 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 723 731 723 731 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 864 872 864 872 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g004">Figure 4</xref>
Pairwise comparisons between FOG-2 and FTR-1 reveal a highly diverged C-terminal region encoded by the final exon (exon 4) (Figure 4A-4C).
