###xml 784 786 784 786 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b32">32</xref>
###xml 787 789 787 789 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b55">55</xref>
###xml 28 39 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 225 236 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 270 281 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 458 469 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Another possibility is that C. briggsae GLD-1 binds and translationally represses an mRNA that promotes spermatogenesis. This could occur if a masculinizing sex determination gene, either present in both species or unique to C. briggsae, has come under GLD-1 control in C. briggsae. Given the conservation of GLD-1 and its regulation of at least some common targets (e.g., rme-2) it is unlikely that changes in GLD-1 are responsible for a new mRNA target in C. briggsae. Instead, it is more likely that one or more new target mRNAs have acquired sequences that direct GLD-1 binding and translational repression. The requirements for GLD-1 binding are only just being elucidated, with a hexanucleotide sequence being one important feature amid otherwise diverse GLD-1 binding regions [32,55]. Thus, small numbers of changes in UTRs are likely to be sufficient for new mRNAs to come under GLD-1-mediated regulation.
###end p 62
###begin title 63
Evolution of Self-Fertile Hermaphroditism
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 80 94 80 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 174 175 174 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b05">5</xref>
###xml 176 177 176 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b06">6</xref>
###xml 178 179 178 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b07">7</xref>
###xml 180 182 180 182 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b10">10</xref>
###xml 183 185 183 185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b11">11</xref>
###xml 186 188 186 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b60">60</xref>
###xml 309 314 309 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 355 365 355 365 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 370 381 370 381 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 550 564 550 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 355 365 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 370 381 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Current phylogenetic data suggest that hermaphroditism evolved independently in Caenorhabditis and other lineages of Rhabditid nematodes from an ancestral female/male state [5,6,7,10,11,60]. This is consistent with our results showing that control of hermaphrodite spermatogenesis at the level of FOG-2/GLD-1/tra-2 mRNA is fundamentally different between C. elegans and C. briggsae. This raises the question, how might the transition from the ancestral female/male to hermaphrodite/male system of reproduction have occurred multiple times within the Caenorhabditis clade?
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 43 53 43 53 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 209 211 209 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b14">14</xref>
###xml 212 214 212 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b61">61</xref>
###xml 215 217 215 217 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b62">62</xref>
###xml 394 396 394 396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b62">62</xref>
###xml 397 399 397 399 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b63">63</xref>
###xml 504 515 504 515 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 520 530 520 530 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. remanei</named-content>
###xml 598 600 598 600 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b63">63</xref>
###xml 601 603 601 603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b64">64</xref>
###xml 631 645 631 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 43 53 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 504 515 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 520 530 <span type="species:ncbi:31234">C. remanei</span>
The anatomy and reproductive physiology of C. elegans allow both sperm that is introduced by mating and sperm that develops within the female gonad of the hermaphrodite to be effectively used in reproduction [14,61,62]. Either source of sperm generates a MSP-derived signal that is required for full-grown oocytes to undergo meiotic maturation, ovulation, and fertilization in the spermatheca [62,63]. Not only is the anatomy conserved but an MSP-derived sperm signal also appears to be utilized by both C. briggsae and C. remanei (a female/male species) to induce oocyte maturation and ovulation [63,64]. This conservation within Caenorhabditis indicates that major changes in anatomy and reproductive physiology are not necessary in the transition from female/male to hermaphrodite/male reproduction.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 103 113 103 113 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 331 333 331 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b65">65</xref>
###xml 558 566 558 566 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0030006-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 581 583 581 583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b18">18</xref>
###xml 584 586 584 586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b19">19</xref>
###xml 587 589 587 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b26">26</xref>
###xml 590 592 590 592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b66">66</xref>
###xml 678 688 678 688 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 742 749 742 749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0030006-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 775 777 775 777 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b20">20</xref>
###xml 778 780 778 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b27">27</xref>
###xml 781 783 781 783 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b28">28</xref>
###xml 784 786 784 786 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b29">29</xref>
###xml 787 789 787 789 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b66">66</xref>
###xml 790 792 790 792 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b67">67</xref>
###xml 793 795 793 795 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b68">68</xref>
###xml 796 798 796 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b69">69</xref>
###xml 815 820 815 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 1043 1048 1043 1048 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 1055 1061 1055 1061 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3-</italic>
###xml 1065 1072 1065 1072 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0030006-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 1397 1403 1397 1403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-1-</italic>
###xml 1407 1412 1407 1412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
###xml 1417 1424 1417 1424 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0030006-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 1531 1541 1531 1541 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 103 113 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 678 688 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1531 1541 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The relative ease with which mutants and mutant combinations can alter the sex determination system in C. elegans has suggested that transitions between mating systems may not be difficult and that the overall sex determination pathway reflects selection for a particular mating system rather than a constant regulatory mechanism [65]. The hermaphrodite pattern of spermatogenesis first then oogenesis is achieved by high masculinizing/low feminizing activity in early larvae followed by low masculinizing/high feminizing activity in late larvae/adults (see Figure 1; reviewed in [18,19,26,66]). Lowering or eliminating germline masculinizing activity in XX animals can convert C. elegans from hermaphrodite/male to female/male reproduction (Table 3, and references therein [20,27,28,29,66,67,68,69]). For example, fog-2-null mutations result in strains that reproduce as XX females and XO males. The mutant female/male strains can be converted back to hermaphrodite reproduction by introducing masculinizing mutations in certain genes (e.g., fog-2-null; fem-3-gf; Table 3). The generality of high masculinizing/low feminizing activity early followed by low masculinizing/high feminizing activity late is borne out by other sets of mutually suppressing feminizing-plus-masculinizing combinations in which the double mutants are self-fertile while each single mutant is usually self-sterile (e.g., tra-1-gf; fem-3-gf; Table 3). Thus, multiple genetic states can yield self-fertile hermaphrodite/male and male/female reproduction in C. elegans.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 103 117 103 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 635 637 635 637 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b70">70</xref>
###xml 758 765 758 765 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0030006-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 855 865 855 865 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 870 881 870 881 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 855 865 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 870 881 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Given the conservation of anatomy and reproductive physiology, an initial conversion from an ancestral Caenorhabditis female/male species to a hermaphrodite/male mode of reproduction may only require a genetic event that results in a transient increase in germline masculinizing activity in early larvae to produce sperm. As long as this change does not interfere with the higher level of feminizing activity (oogenesis) in late larvae/adults, self fertility would be possible. After the establishment of self fertility, there would likely be strong selection for additional genetic events that would optimize self-fertile brood size [70] and result in a clean transition from sperm to oocyte development so that wasteful intersexual gametes are not formed (Table 3). Thus, it is very likely that multiple genetic events now define the differences in the C. elegans and C. briggsae germline sex determination pathways.
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 3 14 3 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans,</italic>
###xml 275 287 275 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae;</italic>
###xml 375 385 375 385 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 390 402 390 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 424 429 424 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 495 506 495 506 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 511 521 511 521 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 564 574 564 574 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 726 736 726 736 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 927 934 927 934 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0030006-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 1024 1035 1024 1035 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans,</italic>
###xml 1302 1313 1302 1313 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 1343 1349 1343 1349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2,</italic>
###xml 3 13 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 275 286 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 375 385 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 390 401 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 495 506 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 511 521 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 564 574 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 726 736 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1024 1034 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1302 1313 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
In C. elegans, the relative levels of TRA-2 feminizing to FEM-3 masculinizing activity appear to be the major regulatory point for the sperm-then-oocyte pattern. There is no a priori reason for TRA-2 or FEM-3 to be the major focus of regulation to achieve hermaphroditism in C. briggsae; if one of these is the focus, then at least some of the regulation must differ between C. elegans and C. briggsae, given the absence of fog-2 and the changed role of GLD-1. Since the last common ancestor of C. briggsae and C. elegans must have contained orthologs of 30 of 31 C. elegans sex determination genes, a change in the regulation of one or more of these genes might be responsible. Alternatively, since much of the regulation of C. elegans germline sex determination is by translational control, mutations in UTRs of mRNAs may result in new genes coming under the control of GLD-1 or another RNA sex determination gene regulator (Table 1). Additionally, duplication and divergence, analogous to what we have found for FOG-2 in C. elegans, may have resulted in a new gene being incorporated into the germline sex determination pathway. To move beyond speculation, the forward genetic analysis currently in progress (R. Ellis and E. Haag, personal communication) will be important for the identification of C. briggsae-specific genes, analogous to fog-2, that are necessary for self-fertile hermaphroditism.
###end p 68
###begin title 69
Materials and Methods
###end title 69
###begin title 70

###end title 70
###begin title 71
Sex determination pathway conservation
###end title 71
###begin p 72
###xml 35 45 35 45 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 123 134 123 134 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 403 414 403 414 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 462 472 462 472 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 528 539 528 539 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 584 595 584 595 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 614 625 614 625 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 674 677 674 677 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;50</sup>
###xml 727 737 727 737 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 820 823 820 823 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;20</sup>
###xml 1303 1313 1303 1313 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 1318 1329 1318 1329 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 1532 1542 1532 1542 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 1546 1557 1546 1557 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 35 45 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 123 134 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 403 414 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 462 472 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 528 539 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 584 595 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 614 625 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 727 737 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1303 1313 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1318 1329 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 1532 1542 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1546 1557 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Protein coding sequences of cloned C. elegans sex determination genes were obtained from Wormbase (; WormPep release 112). C. briggsae genomic sequence was obtained from The Sanger Institute (Cambridge, United Kingdom) or the Genome Sequencing Center (St. Louis, Missouri, United States), and protein sequences were obtained from either Wormbase or Ensemble (; version 17.25.1). Best BLAST orthologs of C. briggsae sex determination proteins were obtained using C. elegans sex determination protein sequences as queries against C. briggsae predicted proteins and six-frame translated C. briggsae genomic sequence. C. briggsae proteins obtained at an e-value cutoff of 1 x 10-50 reciprocal best hits were recovered for 26 of 31 C. elegans proteins. NOS-1 and XOL-1 orthologs were identified at an e-value cutoff of 1 x 10-20 and were also reciprocal best BLAST hits between species. In each case a single reciprocal best hit was identified for each component of the sex determination pathway with the exception of FBF-1 and FBF-2, which returned the same best BLAST hit, and FOG-2. Searches of the non-redundant National Center for Biotechnology Information protein database (GenBank CDS+PDB+SwissProt+PIR+WormPep) with full-length FOG-2 as query revealed only weak similarity to the F-box motif for non-C. elegans or -C. briggsae sequences. Using the highly diverged C-terminal end of FOG-2, including a portion of the Duf38/FTH, or the GLD-1 interaction region of FOG-2 as query did not reveal any hits below an e-value of 0.01 in C. elegans or C. briggsae other than FOG-2 and FTR-1.
###end p 72
###begin title 73
Identification of FTR family members
###end title 73
###begin p 74
###xml 109 111 109 111 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 114 124 114 124 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 374 376 374 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b35">35</xref>
###xml 390 401 390 401 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 479 496 479 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans, fog-2</italic>
###xml 510 515 510 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ftr-1</italic>
###xml 114 124 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 390 401 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 479 489 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
FTR family members are defined by the presence of an N-terminal F-box and C-terminal Duf38/FTH domain (FTR) [25]. C. elegans FTR family members were identified using FOG-2 as a query against WormPep release 112. Each potential FTR was scanned for an N-terminal F-box motif and C-terminal Duf38/FTH domain using the hidden Markov models (HMMs) for each domain (HMMER 2.3.2) [35]. Similarly, C. briggsae FTR family members were identified using FOG-2 as a BLAST query and HMMs. In C. elegans, fog-2 (Y113G7B.5), ftr-1 (Y113G7B.4), CE35646 (Y113G7B.1), CE24144 (Y113G7B.3), CE23289 (Y113G7B.6), and CE23288 (Y113G7B.7) are closely related and tightly linked on Chromosome 5. CE35646 was not included in later analysis because of a divergent N-terminal structure.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 90 100 90 100 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. remanei</named-content>
###xml 337 347 337 347 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. remanei</named-content>
###xml 367 377 367 377 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 430 442 430 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae.</italic>
###xml 518 542 518 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans, C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 547 557 547 557 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. remanei</named-content>
###xml 597 607 597 607 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. remanei</named-content>
###xml 643 653 643 653 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. remanei</named-content>
###xml 90 100 <span type="species:ncbi:31234">C. remanei</span>
###xml 337 347 <span type="species:ncbi:31234">C. remanei</span>
###xml 367 377 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 430 441 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 518 528 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 530 541 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 547 557 <span type="species:ncbi:31234">C. remanei</span>
###xml 597 607 <span type="species:ncbi:31234">C. remanei</span>
###xml 643 653 <span type="species:ncbi:31234">C. remanei</span>
An FTR family also appears to be present and expanded in the obligate male/female species C. remanei based on the currently sequence assembly (Genome Sequencing Center, Washington University, St. Louis, Missouri, United States; 16 September 2004, BLASTn and tBLASTn; ). Our preliminary analysis suggests that closest FOG-2 homologs from C. remanei have diverged from C. elegans approximately to the same level as the FTR genes in C. briggsae. A comprehensive phylogenetic analysis to resolve the relationships between C. elegans, C. briggsae, and C. remanei FTR family members will await accurate C. remanei protein predictions and a complete C. remanei assembly.
###end p 75
###begin title 76
Sequence alignments and analysis
###end title 76
###begin p 77
###xml 175 177 175 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b71">71</xref>
###xml 178 180 178 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b72">72</xref>
###xml 286 297 286 297 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 310 320 310 320 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 640 642 640 642 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b47">47</xref>
###xml 1452 1454 1452 1454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b73">73</xref>
###xml 286 297 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 310 320 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Alignments were generated using CLUSTALW, and conserved residues were identified with the Lasergene MEGALIGN (DNASTAR, Madison, Wisconsin, United States) package and Dialign [71,72], which was also used to identify conserved regions for subsequent phylogenetic analysis. The best BLAST C. briggsae hit to each C. elegans FTR protein used in the phylogeny was included in order to identify any potential one-to-one orthologous pairs along the FOG-2 branch. Non-homologous N- and C-terminal extensions were trimmed, and extremely distant family members unlikely to be functional FOG-2 orthologs were excluded to avoid long branch attraction [47]. Phylogenetic inference was performed using the neighbor-joining (neighbor) program in the PHYLIP package (Phylogeny Inference Package version 3.5c; Department of Genetics, University of Washington, Seattle, Washington, United States) using the BLOSUM45 distance matrix. Trees with and without gaps were generated, and comparison revealed some differences in branching order, but only within the species. For the tree presented here, positions with gaps were excluded and all non-homologous or highly divergent sequences trimmed. The topology of the tree structure was tested by bootstrapping with 1,000 replicates and by analysis of the alignment using protpars from the PHYLIP package (a maximum parsimony method), which produced a tree with a similar branching order. Trees were processed using TreeView [73].
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 33 34 33 34 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 36 37 36 37 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 277 278 277 278 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 284 285 284 285 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 297 299 297 299 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b74">74</xref>
###xml 341 343 341 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b52">52</xref>
###xml 406 408 406 408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b53">53</xref>
Codon-restricted alignments for Ka/Ks calculation were generated using Se-Al (a sequence alignment editor by A. Rambaut, version 2; available at ) to modify CLUSTALW-aligned cDNA or predicted cDNA sequences, and all gaps and frame-shifted regions were removed. Sliding-window Ka and Ks estimates [74] were generated using DNASP (version 3) [52], and codon-based analysis was performed using PAML (codeml) [53] (HKY substitution model) to confirm the presence of codons under positive selection (95% confidence) within the sliding windows.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
Worm culture and RNAi
###end title 79
###begin p 80
###xml 0 10 0 10 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 45 56 45 56 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 87 101 87 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>
###xml 218 234 218 234 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Escherichia coli</named-content>
###xml 294 296 288 290 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b75">75</xref>
###xml 334 344 328 338 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 349 360 343 354 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 398 400 392 394 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b54">54</xref>
###xml 445 450 439 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1</italic>
###xml 455 460 449 454 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-3</italic>
###xml 0 10 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 45 56 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 218 239 <span type="species:ncbi:637912">Escherichia coli OP50</span>
###xml 334 344 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 349 360 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
C. elegans (N2, Bristol, United Kingdom) and C. briggsae (AF16) were obtained from the Caenorhabditis Genetics Center University of Minnesota, Minneapolis, Minnesota, United States. Cultures of both were maintained on Escherichia coli OP50 on NGM plates at 20 degreesC as previously described [75]. RNAi was performed by injection in C. elegans and C. briggsae essentially as described previously [54]. Double-stranded RNAs for species-specific gld-1 and fog-3 were generated by PCR amplification of cDNA with SP6 (5') and T7 (3') linkers, gel purified, sequenced, and used in RNA synthesis reaction using the appropriate Ambion kit (MEGAscript SP6 or T7; Austin, Texas, United States). Double-stranded RNAs were injected at 0.5 mg/ml into young adult N2 animals and F1 progeny collected 12-48 h post injection and matured to 24 h post L4 stage before gonads were dissected, fixed, and stained to score for abnormal phenotypes.
###end p 80
###begin title 81
Staining
###end title 81
###begin p 82
###xml 43 53 43 53 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 58 69 58 69 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 216 218 216 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b29">29</xref>
###xml 219 221 219 221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b30">30</xref>
###xml 43 53 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 58 69 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 242 248 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 309 314 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Dissection, antibody, and DAPI staining of C. elegans and C. briggsae gonads were performed essentially as previously described with fixation in 3% formaldehyde, 80% methanol, and 100 mM dibasic potassium phosphate [29,30]. Affinity purified rabbit polyclonal anti-GLD-1 antibodies were used at 1:50, and MSP mouse monoclonal antibody was used at 1:2,000, both with overnight incubation at room temperature (anti-MSP antibody was the kind gift of M. Kosinski and D. Greenstein, Vanderbilt University School of Medicine, Nashville, Tennessee, United States). Texas Red or Alexa488 secondary antibodies were used to detect staining, and DAPI was used visualize DNA morphology. Epifluorescent images were captured with a Zeiss (Oberkochen, Germany) Axioskop coupled to a Hamamatsu Photonics (Hamamatsu City, Japan) digital CCD camera, and processed with Photoshop 7.0 (Adobe, San Jose, California, United States). All image post-processing (brightness, contrast, pseudo-color, unsharp mask) was performed identically for each image.
###end p 82
###begin title 83
Constructs and transformation
###end title 83
###begin p 84
###xml 88 90 88 90 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 913 915 913 915 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b76">76</xref>
###xml 916 918 916 918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b77">77</xref>
###xml 16 21 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 425 430 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
GLD-1 and FOG-2 yeast two-hybrid binding assays were performed as previously described [25] with the inclusion of 20 mM 3-amino-triazole. Progressive C-terminal deletions in FOG-2 and FTR-1/FOG-2 chimeric constructs were generated using PCR amplification of the appropriate coding sequences (FOG-2 full-length [327 aa], 318 aa, 299 aa, 263 aa, or exon 4 [251aa], or FTR-1 full-length [318 aa]) and cloned by recombination in yeast. In each case GLD-1 was used as bait in the pAS1 vector (DNA binding) and FOG-2 deletion constructs in the pACTII vector (activation). FOG-2 was found to exhibit low levels of auto-activation in the pAS1 (DNA binding) vector, so binding assays were performed in only one direction to avoid background and using high levels of 3-amino-triazole. The constructs were sequenced, and the Skp1-related F-box-binding protein SKR-1 (in pAS1) was used as a positive control for interaction [76,77].
###end p 84

Homologs of the Caenorhabditis elegans masculinizing gene her-1 in C. briggsae and the filarial parasite Brugia malayi

###begin p 197
###xml 136 141 136 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 146 151 146 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
###xml 183 188 183 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 222 227 222 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 232 238 232 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1,</italic>
###xml 282 287 282 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 292 298 292 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1,</italic>
###xml 327 332 327 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 550 555 550 555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 560 565 560 565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1</italic>
###xml 601 606 601 606 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 656 662 656 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3,</italic>
###xml 753 758 753 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>
###xml 763 768 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gld-1</italic>
###xml 794 799 794 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 831 837 831 837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3,</italic>
###xml 875 880 875 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 881 886 881 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-3</italic>
(A) Genetic pathway for gene activity, where arrows represent positive regulation and bars represent negative regulation. The key genes tra-2 and fem-3 and the upstream regulators of tra-2 that are the focus of this work, fog-2 and gld-1, are in large bold font. The upstream genes fog-2 and gld-1, which are key regulators of tra-2 and addressed in this work, are also in large bold font. The gene activities at each level in the hierarchy are indicated below as "ACTIVE" in bold or "inactive" in grey. In L3 and L4 hermaphrodites the activities of fog-2 and gld-1 are high, leading to repression of tra-2 activity (also see [B]) and the de-repression of fem-3, resulting in the onset of spermatogenesis. In L4 and adult hermaphrodites the activity of fog-2 and gld-1 are low, leading to high tra-2 activity and the repression of fem-3, resulting in oogenesis. The shift in tra-2/fem-3 balance allows for the switch from spermatogenesis to oogenesis in an otherwise female somatic gonad in the hermaphrodite.
###end p 197
###begin p 198
###xml 4 14 4 14 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 27 32 27 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 152 157 152 157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 164 166 164 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b25">25</xref>
###xml 199 204 199 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 314 316 314 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b32">32</xref>
###xml 317 319 317 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0030006-b34">34</xref>
###xml 4 14 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
(B) C. elegans FOG-2/GLD-1/tra-2 mRNA ternary complex. Current data indicates that FOG-2 and GLD-1 are required for the translational repression of the tra-2 mRNA [25]. GLD-1 binds as a dimer to the tra-2 mRNA 3'UTR at two 28 nucleotide direct repeat elements (TGE/DRE, blocks) and FOG-2 makes contact with GLD-1 [32,34]. All three components are required for the proper specification of hermaphrodite spermatogenesis.
###end p 198

###begin p 200
###xml 51 61 51 61 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 66 77 66 77 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 151 161 151 161 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 166 177 166 177 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 348 369 348 369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 394 404 394 404 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 429 440 429 440 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 633 642 633 642 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="sg001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 790 800 790 800 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 1070 1079 1070 1079 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="sg002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 51 61 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 66 77 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 151 161 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 166 177 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 394 404 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 429 440 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 790 800 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
A radial phylogram showing the relationships of 30 C. elegans and C. briggsae FTR genes closely related to FOG-2 was generated using neighbor-joining. C. elegans and C. briggsae protein predictions with complete F-box and Duf38/FTH (FTR proteins) were identified using BLAST and HMMs, aligned using CLUSTALW, trimmed, de-gapped, and realigned (see Materials and Methods). A clear separation of C. elegans (below dashed line) and C. briggsae (above dashed line) FTR proteins is indicated by the phylogeny. The branch containing FOG-2 and FTR-1 is in bold. Tree is unrooted, and branch lengths are proportional to divergence (also see Figure S1). Bar represents 0.1 substitutions per site. FOG-2 and FTR-1, across their entire length, are more similar to each other than to any other gene in C. elegans. Comparison of the diverged approximately 40aa C-terminal region from both proteins to the closely related FTR genes in the FOG-2 cluster reveals 48% average pairwise identity between these FTRs and FTR-1 and 22% average pairwise identify between these FTRs and FOG-2 (Figure S2). One interpretation of this greater similarity is that FTR-1 may be ancestral; however, it is not clear whether the slight increase in similarity over about 40aa is significant or whether selection rather than evolutionary history produced the sequence similarity observed.
###end p 200

###xml 117 119 117 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ce</italic>
###xml 120 125 120 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-2</italic>
###xml 146 151 146 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fem-2</italic>
###xml 221 237 221 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans fog-2</italic>
###xml 245 253 245 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ce_fog-2</italic>
###xml 275 280 275 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fog-2</italic>

###xml 843 851 843 851 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="st002">Table S2</xref>
###xml 19 30 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 166 176 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 331 342 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 642 653 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 693 704 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 786 796 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Each gene from the C. briggsae contig with an ortholog defined as a reciprocal best BLAST hit is present on both maps (B and C), and blocks of synteny defined by the C. elegans organization are in the same color. Only one (Y113G7B.11) of the 22 genes from the 82.6-kb fog-2 cluster was found to have a reciprocal best BLAST hit in C. briggsae (contig cb25.fpc0129, corresponding to the predicted gene CBG05618; Table S1). No FTR genes or genes related to those in the fog-2 cluster were found within 50-kb on either side of CBG05618, indicating that this region does not share conserved synteny with the fog-2 cluster. Instead, the potential C. briggsae ortholog of Y113G7B.11 is located on a C. briggsae contig region that shows extensive conserved synteny with a different portion of C. elegans Chromosome 5 not involving the fog-2 cluster (Table S2).

###begin p 211
###xml 727 748 727 748 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 764 774 764 774 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 779 790 779 790 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 73 78 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 764 774 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 779 790 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
(D) The C-terminal FOG-2 region is required for GLD-1 interaction in the yeast two-hybrid system. Full-length FOG-2 (black) and FTR-1 (grey) constructs were tested for interaction with GLD-1. FOG-2 interacts with GLD-1 (++++) whereas FTR-1 does not (-). Progressive C-terminal deletions (black) in FOG-2 were generated to identify FOG-2 requirements for GLD-1 interaction. Binding to GLD-1 was completely eliminated with the removal of the C-terminal 64 aa of FOG-2 exon 4. Transfer of exon 4 to FTR-1 (grey/black chimera) resulted in the transfer of GLD-1 binding to FTR-1. Control interactions to test for the production of functional proteins were performed with the Skp1 homolog SKR-1, which binds to the F-box region (see Materials and Methods). Searches for C. elegans and C. briggsae proteins with homology to the 64-aa FOG-2 region required for GLD-1 interaction (or FOG-2 exon 4) failed to identify any predicted proteins with significant homology (>35% or e-value = 0.01) other than FTR-1, which cannot bind GLD-1 and does not compensate for FOG-2 in sex determination.

(A) RNAi of C. briggsae gld-1 results in masculinization of the germline. Paired DAPI-stained (left) and GLD-1- and MSP-stained (right) images of dissected young adult hermphrodite germlines. Top four panels illustrate the similarity between C. elegans and C. briggsae germline morphology and polarity (DAPI, blue; GLD-1, green; MSP, red). In both species, sperm ("sperm" arrow) are produced first before switching to oogenesis ("oocytes" arrow), and the pattern of cytoplasmic GLD-1 accumulation (green) is identical. GFP-injected controls were identical to wild-type animals. C. briggsae gld-1 RNAi animals exhibit masculinization of the germline (lower panels). A vast excess of sperm extends to the loop region ("sperm" arrows), and spermatogenesis extends further distally (solid line). Masculinization is confirmed by a corresponding extension in MSP staining beyond the loop (compare lower right to controls above).

"Percent Length" is the extent of alignable sequence. All proteins with the exception of fog-2 returned reciprocal best BLAST hits in C. elegans and C. briggsae. Proteins that contain RNA-binding motifs or that function in RNA regulation are the following: ATX-2, FOX-1, FOG-1, FOG-2, GLD-1, GLD-3, NOS-1, NOS-2, NOS-3, FBF-1, FBF-2, MOG-1, MOG-4, MOG-5, and MOG-6

###begin title 227
###xml 0 10 0 10 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 0 10 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
C. elegans Sex Determination Mutants That Yield Female/Male Reproduction and Mutually Suppressed Hermaphrodite Reproduction
###end title 227
###begin p 228
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sup>
a gf, gain of function; Mog, allele(s) show a masculinization of the germline phenotype; Fog, allele(s) show a feminization of the germline phenotype; Fem, allele(s) show a feminization of the soma and germline phenotype; ts, temperature sensitive; lf, loss of function, in these cases non-null
###end p 228
###begin p 229
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</sup>
b All of the masculinizing and feminizing mutant combinations that show mutual suppression display the pattern of sperm first then oocytes as in wild-type. The opposite pattern, oocytes first then sperm, would not result in self fertility and thus would not be reproductively successful. The reason that these mutant combinations all display the wild-type pattern, instead of the oocyte then sperm pattern, is unclear and suggests that an additional level of sex determination pathway regulation remains to be uncovered
###end p 229
###begin p 230
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</sup>
c Mutually suppressing feminizing and masculinizing double-mutant hermaphrodites often have intersexual germ cells between the sperm and oocytes, unlike wild-type hermaphrodites
###end p 230
###begin p 231
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sup>
d Embryos generated showed developmental arrest
###end p 231

###end p 232
